## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship in materials, which is fundamental to constitutive modeling. Temperature typically softens materials (reducing modulus and flow stress), while strain can cause hardening, and their interplay governs thermomechanical behavior.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law with temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon-type strain hardening)
- Power-law hardening with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (strain hardening with Arrhenius-type thermal effect)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * epsilon**c2) (nonlinear stress-strain with hardening transition)
- Johnson-Cook strength model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T)**c4 (combined strain hardening and thermal softening)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon))) * exp(c3 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal effect)
- Linear thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - T) (modulus linearly decreasing with temperature)
- Polynomial thermal modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (quadratic temperature dependence of elastic modulus)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power-law hardening for pre-strained materials)
- Thermal softening with homologous temperature: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - c2 * T**c3) (power-law softening in temperature)
- Hyperbolic sine creep law: sigma = c0 * arcsinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * T)) (Garofalo-type high-temperature deformation)
- Combined linear-nonlinear: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 + c3 * T (additive elastic, plastic, and thermal contributions)
- Exponential saturation hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * (1 + c2 * T) (Voce-type with linear thermal coupling)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or exp(-c*T) applied to stress
- Strain hardening saturation → Terms like (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) indicating Voce-type asymptotic hardening
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon**c with 0 < c < 1 representing diminishing hardening rate (Hollomon behavior)
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 in sigma = c0 + f(epsilon) representing initial yield strength
- Multiplicative separability → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T) when strain and temperature effects are decoupled
- Polynomial temperature dependence of modulus → Quadratic or cubic polynomials in T multiplying strain terms
- Transition from elastic to plastic regime → Piecewise-like behavior approximated by smooth functions like tanh(c*epsilon) or rational forms
- High-temperature activated deformation → Arrhenius-type exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T) factors capturing thermally activated processes
